Date:  Tue, 01 Jan 2008 17:44:37 -0500
From:  KCStarguy@aol.com
Subject:  Star of Bethlehem and SNPro
clickable links are on my blog
(E.O.A.S.blog) http://eoas-dreric1kansas.blogspot.com/
**
A few years ago, I researched the subject of the Star of Bethlehem for a
presentation I was doing in Kansas City, KS. I pointed to 10 different
possibitilies, omens, events, astronomical phenomenon. My presentation was entitled "The
10 Myths of the Star of Bethlehem".

It wasn't Halley's Comet which appeared in sky 12BC ( this was thought to be
too late ).
Besides comets were  bad omens and mostly associated with dread. .

http://clioaudio.com/2007/12/24/nero-and-the-comets-of-doom/

This nice account tries to explain comet as the "Star" (blog info on
12/23/2007)
http://www.sciencemusings.com/2007/12/star-of-bethlehem.html

another

http://nation.ittefaq.com/issues/2007/12/25/news0558.htm

Mark Kidger of the European Space Agency (as did I ) that while a Triple
Conjuction in 7BC was good (an forthcoming omen), the conjunction of 2 BC was a
possibly better or best fit.

Going back in time, with my Imac Macintosh computer and  Starry Night Pro
software, I simulated this conjunction. There it was in 2BC. I concluded that it
was this conjunction after looking at a host of other possibilities.

But lately Kidger and others have surmised that this date may have been too
late for the "Star". So that led to something in between.

Now the suggestion turned to a possibility of a nova star in 5 BC. This is in
the realm of one of my ten possibilities.

http://www.baltimoresun.com/news/local/bal-te.md.christmas
25dec25,0,822279.story?coll=bal_tab01_layout

Astronomers are still looking for this Nova that the Chinese might have noted
and that might have been a good candidate.

Happy holidays!

Date:  Fri, 04 Jan 2008 11:51:27 -0600
From:  Curious George 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] Comet C/2006 S% (Hill) 2008.01.02
Apologies for the OT, but this is something that needs to be understood by
astronomical imagers so I will reply to the group.

What you say is correct, but incomplete in understanding. The levels of
COLORS possible are different between GIF and JPEG. However, the images you
embed on your web pages are not COLOR they are GREYSCALE. (If you were
displaying color images, you must use JPEG if over 256 colors in the scene.)

Shades of grey are reproduced on a computer monitor with Red, Green, and
Blue.
If the intensity of each of those colors is turned all the way up, the
resulting pixel on the monitor is WHITE. If they are turned all the way
down, the pixel is BLACK. To produce the different levels of GREY, the Red,
Green, and Blue must be at exactly the same intensity (any variance and you
don't have grey, you have some color).

This means that a 24-bit computer monitor is capable of producing
16,777,216 COLORS,
but only 254 shades of GREY (plus Black and White).

Therefore the point of my question. If the image is greyscale, saving it as
a JPG for web page use results in a larger filesize and corresponding longer
download time (and bandwidth usage) over saving it as a GIF.

For a fuller explanation:
http://training.stisd.net/tutorials/PhotoshopCSFoundation/section4/lesson4.4c.htm

Bottom line: For what you are doing there IS NO increase in quality of the
greyscale image in saving it as a JPEG over GIF.

I hope this provides a fuller explanation for those who may not have
understood the reason for my question.

Date:  Sat, 05 Jan 2008 21:52:58 -0500
From:  KCStarguy@aol.com
Subject:  comet observations from Kansas

It was a spectacular night. I went down to Powell Obervatory (Louisbourg, KS
south of Kansas City) and use the 30 inch telescope.

at 10:16 pm :
8p Tuttle looked fine and seemed to have a ghostly greenish coma with a nice
nucleus. But those green comets are so hard to see eventhough with this
telescope and this being the closest approach to Earth at that encounter. It seemed
to have a ghostly faint coma around the nucleus near either TYC1205-1195-1 or
TYC1205-363-1. I was surprised it was not brighter. Seemed to have a pulsing
shroud around the nucleus but faint.

Holmes was nice but remarkable unlike Tuttle easier to see with naked eye.

Mars (with its canyon) and Saturn (the ring were spectacular).

Dr. Eric Flescher (kcstarguy@aol.com), Olathe, KS: Comet Observers Award
Coordinator- Astronomical League / Astronomical Society of Kansas, KC,

Date:  Sat, 12 Jan 2008 15:35:52 -0600
From:  "P. Clay Sherrod" 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] 29P OUTBURST
Comet 29P has been up to magnitude 11.5 to 12.8 for about a week and seems to be fairly
steady at this time. Not quite an outburst, but a very nice brightening. You will note
that the comet is considerably asymmetrical at this time, with a considerably flattened
eastern coma with a fairly nice amount of structural detail visible opposite that.

Clay
-------------
Dr. P. Clay Sherrod
Arkansas Sky Observatories
Harvard MPC/ H43 (Conway)
Harvard MPC/ H41 (Petit Jean Mountain)
Harvard MPC/ H45 (Petit Jean Mtn. South)
http://www.arksky.org/

There is no DSO at this position.

There is also nothing visible in an image of David Bender at this
position that was taken just some min before yours:
http://kometen.fg-vds.de/pix/17P.htm
http://kometen.fg-vds.de/pix/17P/17P_1_10012008.htm

So I would guess its a reflection of Algol which would fit roughly.

Date:  Mon, 14 Jan 2008 00:38:17 +0100
From:  Wolfgang Renz 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] Something in My Images of 17P, also???
Hi Mark

Do you mean that diffuse blue blotches in the:
- mid upper left of your Nov 12th images ?
- mid upper right of your Jan 12th images ?

These are probably reflections of Mirfak and Algol.
The middle of the connecting lines between the blotches and
stars stay at the same position relative to the center of the
image.

Clear skies
Wolfgang

--
Wolfgang Renz, Karlsruhe, Germany

Date:  Tue, 15 Jan 2008 08:24:56 -0600
From:  "P. Clay Sherrod" 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] 29P
Via CCD this morning (Jan 15 U.T.) with exposures just long enough for saturation (i.e.,
10 sec or less) we were able to obtain calibrated magnitude estimates (R) of 10.3 to
10.5 of 29P using a field star (UCAC-2) of magnitude 10.3; note that the "egg-shape" of
this comet is very, very reminiscent of the pre-outburst/splintering phase of this comet
before the last remarkable breakup, and I would urge observers to monitor this comet
very closely for the next two weeks.

Clay
-------------
Dr. P. Clay Sherrod
Arkansas Sky Observatories
Harvard MPC/ H43 (Conway)
Harvard MPC/ H41 (Petit Jean Mountain)
Harvard MPC/ H45 (Petit Jean Mtn. South)
http://www.arksky.org/

Date:  Thu, 17 Jan 2008 23:28:39 -0000
From:  tricks46 
Subject:  17P-29P Outburst.
Hello. In the future when possible I will add to these two outburst
recorded with the same equipment about 3 days after the reported
events. This image shows the first two, 17p and 29p, taken with the
same scope, camera, processing, equipment, exposures and scale about
equal for each image. The only real difference is 29p has been
enlarged from the original by 2.5x or close with both taken with a 1x1
bin. The distance of the comets at the reported outburst time was;
17p - 2007/10/27 - Earth distance 1.63 au - Sun distance 2.44 au - 29P -
2008/01/15 - Earth distance 5.08 au - Sun distance 5.98 au. Image in
the top right is the original turned negative with center having a hard
histogram applied and the top left the negative with further
processing.
Remember this is only for viewing the similar things if any and not
science. Just seems outburst are somewhat common and I wanted my own
record for these 2 comets and future outburst of other comets.
Thanks
Mike H.

http://fototime.com/537AFD0EFD29A23/orig.jpg

Date:  Tue, 26 Feb 2008 05:47:33 +0100
From:  Wolfgang Renz 
Subject:  Re: asteroid over ic 410 ?
Hello Nico

Its very unlikely that you found a new one that is such bright.

You can check such finding yourself via the:
MPChecker Minor Planet Checker
http://scully.harvard.edu/~cgi/CheckMP
Here you always have the most complete and most current
data which is usually not the case when using a planetarium
software.

Using the shown center position and time on your web page
produces the following list of MPs of IC 410:
<
The following objects, brighter than V = 25.0,
were found in the 25.0-arcminute region around
R.A. = 05 22 47, Decl. = +33 24 05 (J2000.0)
on 2008 02 24.92 UT:
Object designation R.A. Decl. V Offsets Motion/hr Orbit Further observations?
h m s � ' " R.A. Decl. R.A. Decl. Comment (Elong/Decl/V at date 1)
2002 TR168 05 22 37.6 +33 20 26 20.9 2.0W 3.7S 11+ 13- 3o Desirable between 2008 Feb. 25-Mar. 26. (105.5,+33.3,20.9)
(83728) 2001 TH110 05 22 28.5 +33 26 12 20.3 3.9W 2.1N 12+ 7- 7o None needed at this time.
(4417) Lecar 05 22 51.1 +33 30 44 16.7 0.8E 6.7N 14+ 8- 15o None needed at this time.
2001 SY210 05 22 37.0 +33 15 28 20.9 2.1W 8.6S 18+ 7- 4o Very desirable between 2008 Feb. 25-Mar. 26. (105.5,+33.2,20.9)
2003 TY 05 23 15.8 +33 38 07 21.2 6.0E 14.0N 17+ 6- 4o Desirable between 2008 Feb. 25-Mar. 26. (105.6,+33.6,21.2)
(143075) 2002 WP20 05 24 18.1 +33 22 35 21.2 19.0E 1.5S 9+ 1- 5o None needed at this time.
2000 YA81 05 22 26.1 +33 03 43 19.4 4.4W 20.4S 22+ 18+ 3o None needed at this opposition.
(58237) 1993 FR66 05 22 16.3 +33 44 16 19.9 6.4W 20.2N 16+ 9- 9o None needed at this time.
(71670) 2000 EP157 05 21 04.4 +33 31 29 18.7 21.4W 7.4N 36+ 20- 6o None needed at this time.
1995 WK38 05 24 33.4 +33 32 26 21.9 22.2E 8.3N 10+ 5- 3o Desirable between 2008 Feb. 25-Mar. 26. (105.9,+33.5,21.9)
Number of objects checked = 384044
>
So its essential that you search with an accurate coordinate +
mid-time of exposure pair to identify if its one of these.

But first you should always take a look at you single light, bias,
dark and flat frames:

Looking at the Lum images (hor flip, stretch to 3200-5000 ADU):
L-BIN1X1-480S-001.fit ... L-BIN1X1-480S-004.fit
there is no trace of a hot pixel or object on the shown "astroid
track". The visible hot pixel stay pretty much at the same location
(within a very few pixel).
-> If it would be an astroid it should be visible here.

Looking at all available 1x1 images (Lum, NII, OIII):
-> In the 1x1 images there is a close double hot pixel visible at:
(444,932) and (447,933).

Looking at the NII 2x2 images (hor flip) there is something visible at:
file "object" hot pixel star
UNO-BIN2X2-900S-001.fit (222,466) + (223,466) (188,464) (246,486)
UNO-BIN2X2-900S-002.fit (222,466) + (223,466) (188,464) (246,487)
UNO-BIN2X2-900S-003.fit (222,466) + (223,466) (188,464) (244,488)
UNO-BIN2X2-900S-004.fit (222,466) + (223,466) (188,464) (243,490)
Looking at the Ha 2x2 images (hor flip) there is something visible at:
file "object" hot pixel star
DUE-BIN2X2-900S-001.fit (222,466) + (223,466) (188,464) (241,491)
DUE-BIN2X2-900S-002.fit (222,466) + (223,466) (188,464) (240,493)
DUE-BIN2X2-900S-003.fit (222,466) + (223,466) (188,464) (239,494)
-> Its very unprobable that an astroid would move exactly on the
opposite dricetion of your star drift.

-> In the 1x1 images the "object" is clearly visible as a close but
not neighbouring pair of hot pixel.
-> In the 2x2 images the "object" occumies always two horizonally
neighbouring pixel.
-> The "object" is "visible" just in your 2x2 NII and Ha images and
stays at the very same pixel location (like other hot pixel) while
stars slowly drift in x and y. As the drift is higher in x than in y
and there are 2 neighbouring hot pixel, this lifts it above the
detection threshold of your processing.
-> In the 1x1 images is clearly visible as a close pair of hot pixel.

How did you calibrate and process your FITS files to get these
"round moving object" results ?

Did you apply any darks at all ?
Time matching darks or time scaled darks ?

You probably should reconsider your calibration technique to
get rid of all the hot pixel before doing any further processing

Clear skies
Wolfgang

--
Wolfgang Renz, Karlsruhe, Germany
Rz.BAV = WRe.vsnet = RWG.AAVSO

Date:  Mon, 10 Mar 2008 23:14:37 +1100
From:  Dave Herald 
Subject:  Comet 8P Tuttle
I've just posted an image of 8P Tuttle at:
http://tinyurl.com/2rpy4s
taken today (2008 March 10.4) The image shows a very faint ion tail in PA 110 degrees. The
bright object below the comet is a star, and the 'fuzzy' star at top left is an internal
reflection of that star.

The tail is much less pronounced than on 2008 Feb 11.4, which was posted at:
http://tinyurl.com/2on244

Dave Herald
Canberra, Australia

Date:  Tue, 11 Mar 2008 18:07:08 -0000
From:  tricks46 
Subject:  17P-2008/03/11
Hello. Skys were clearing and the Moon was not far away. I took 1 1/2
hrs of information but a bump to the mount rendered most unsuable with
tracking streaks. Even after using a total of 30 minutes rgb filtered
images and changing to the ST10XMEI ccd I almost couldn't see the
comet. It is a much bigger drop with the return of the Moon than I
expected. Someone needs to discover us another big, bright, slow
moving comet
Mike H.

http://fototime.com/93F0AC46E4020E4/orig.jpg

Hello,

I haven't seen many pics of this comet yet, so decided to try it
myself. Well, I did capture it, but the picture isn't either valuable
nor beautiful. Anyway, here goes... comet C/2008 C1 Chen-Gao, taken
with Orion Optics 6" f/5 reflector, Canon 350D unmodified (yet),
3x5mins, ISO1600. Stacked with DeepSkyStacker, using the last sub
(taken at March 10.94 UT) as a reference frame.

Date:  Mon, 31 Mar 2008 10:22:24 -0000
From:  "patrik.trncak" 
Subject:  List of comet images
Dear Comet friends,
My name is Patrik Trncak from the Czech republic and I am interested
in comets images. I have made list of html links of periodic comet
images from all years. I have searched all comets web-sites and PDF
articles on the internet. I have a problem with comets: 5D, 20D, 25D,
34D, 35P, 39P, 83P, 138P, therefore I would like to ask you whether
you could help me with this project? I especially need comets 39P, 83P
and 138P which images I have not found. I think that pictures with
those comets must exist. But where? Note: (in the list) red is
drawings, blue is photo. Title "my personal collection file" are
pictures not available on the internet, but I can send them to you, if
you want. My list is here:
http://hvezdarna-holesov.wz.cz/periodic_comets.pdf

Date:  Sun, 06 Apr 2008 11:13:47 +1200
From:  John Drummond 
Subject:  Re: [comets-ml] Comet 2007 W1 Boattini obs
Here's a photo of Boattini from Friday 4th April 2008 (.40 UT) through the 16" Newtonian @ f5.2 with an SBIG STL11000M CCD. A nucleus is evident in the photo, but this is probably a by product of processing - as I also couldn't clearly see a nucleus through my other 16" (Dob)...

1 minute sub exposures - 5 x luminance, 3 x RGB. The FOV = ~1 degree by .66 degrees.

http://www.possumobservatory.co.nz/comet_boatini-2007w1-41cm@f5,2-1min-5lum-1x1,3rgb-2x2-25c-080404-drummond-web.jpg
or
http://tinyurl.com/6k3nwc

Cheers

John Drummond
Possum Observatory (IAU Code: E94)
Gisborne, New Zealand
E 177° 53', S 38° 38'
Email: john_drummond@xtra.co.nz
Website: http://www.possumobservatory.co.nz
Images: http://www.possumobservatory.co.nz/latest_images-all-continuing.htm

----- Original Message -----
From: David Seargent
To: comets-ml@yahoogroups.com
Sent: Saturday, April 05, 2008 6:03 PM
Subject: Re: [comets-ml] Comet 2007 W1 Boattini obs

Michael Mattiazzo wrote

My visual observation of comet C/2007 W1 Boattini this evening
2008 April 2.40 UT: m1=10.1, Dia.=4', DC=2...25x100mm B...Michael Mattiazzo
(Castlemaine, Victoria)
This comet appears brighter than its predicted ephemeris by nearly a full
magnitude.

Michael and all,

Exactly! In large binoculars, the comet is a good magnitude brighter than predicted. On April 3, I made it 9.9 in a 10-cm binocular telescope at 25x.

But it is very diffuse and without much condensation.

Regards,

David Seargent

Date:  Sun, 27 Apr 2008 18:00:06 +0200
From:  ligustri rolando 
Subject:  Re:  [Comet-Images] equipment and magnification? C/2007 W1
>Nice image . What equipment and magnification did you use for C/2007 W1?
>Dr. Eric Flescher (kcstarguy@aol.com), Olathe, KS: Lat 38.834, Lon -94.778:

Thanks Dr.Flesher.

it is the second time that I use the system G3 of Global Rent a Scope.
I have to say that I find that the system is really fantastic!
he is constituted by an apo 150/1100 and ccd ST10Xme.
for the image I have wanted to use ccd in bin 2, to have a greater sensibility,
considering that I wanted to use some short expositions. however what have seen in these
years of I use, that ago really difference is the quality of the sky! be impressive
really! New Mexico sky is fantastic.
sinned not to so also have a sky where we have us the observatory, in Italy...

regards
Rolando

Date:  Fri, 09 May 2008 23:12:26 +1000
From:  Michael Mattiazzo 
Subject:  comet 2007 W1 Boattini images May 9th 2008

Hi Folks,

I've uploaded images of comet 2007 w1 Boattini from this evening to my
website.

http://www.yp-connect.net/~mmatti/

2008 May 9.48UT.
Left: 3 minute exposure, Canon 300D digital camera. 150mm zoom lens,
cropped.
Right: 10x15 sec, C11 SCT at f/3 + MX7c ccd.
Approximate visual magnitude estimate 6.6

Cheers,
Michael Mattiazzo

From:  rotorzilla_jp 
Subject:  C/2007 W1 Boattini   stereo image
I use a program StereoPhoto Maker to make stereo images. Here is on
of C/2007 W1 Boattini taken 10 minutes apart

this is cross eye stereo image slowly cross your eyes until both
images overlap and form 1 image.

http://heliospheric-labs.com/gallery/d/17091-1/2007w1-d2wf-2008-5-9-stereo.jpg

Tony Farkas
Okinawa, Japan

Date:  Wed, 21 May 2008 22:03:43 +0200
From:  Gerald Rhemann 
Subject:  comet Boattini images taken in Namibia
Hi list,

Here are two images of comet Boattini taken on my recent trip to Namibia.

Unfortunately in the nick of time my website run down :-(

Therefore here are the data:

comet C/2007 W 1 Boattini on April 29:

Telescope: 10" f 3.8 ASA Astrograph

Camera: FLI Microline 8300

Exp.times: 2x180 sec. R, 2x180 sec. G, 3x 180 sec. B

Location: Farm Tivoli, Namibia/SW-Africa

Imager: Gerald Rhemann

HYPERLINK
"http://www.astrostudio.at/RGB-C-2007-W1-Boattini-RGBapril29.jpg"www.astrost
udio.at/RGB-C-2007-W1-Boattini-RGBapril29.jpg

comet C/2007 W 1 Boattini on May 6:

Telescope: 10" f 3.8 ASA Astrograph

Camera: FLI Microline 8300

Exp.times: 2x120 sec. R, 2x120 sec. G, 4x 120 sec. B 2x2 binning

Location: Farm Tivoli, Namibia/SW-Africa

Imager: Gerald Rhemann

HYPERLINK
"http://www.astrostudio.at/comet-boattini-mai6.jpg"www.astrostudio.at/comet-
boattini-mai6.jpg

kind regards

Gerald

Date:  Sat, 31 May 2008 11:36:07 +1200
From:  John Drummond 
Subject:  Comet Boattini (C/2007 W1) image from last night
Hi all,

I imaged Comet Boattini (C/2007 W1) last night (30.29-34 May 2008 UT). I seemed to have picked up a 1? ion tail pointing in a PA of 125? (~SE). It was taken with a 20cm f4.6 Vixen Newtonian. The images were median combined in Maxim DL and processed in Photoshop.

http://www.possumobservatory.co.nz/comet_2007W1-boatinni-20cm@f5,2-1min-16xlum-1x1_8xrgb-2x2-080530-0703-0815UT-drummond.jpg
or
http://tinyurl.com/4v7j7x

IMAGING DETAILS -

TARGET:
Comet Boattini (C/2007 W1)

POSITION:
RA 08h 20m, Dec -25? 26'

MAG and SIZE:
Mag = ~5.2, Diameter = ~20'

IMAGING DATE: 30.29-34 May 2008 (UT)

TELESCOPE:
20cm (8") Vixen Newtonian (eq)

FOCAL LENGTH:
920mm (@f4.6)

CAMERA:
SBIG STL11000M CCD

CHIP:
4008 x 2672 pixels (full 35mm)

PIXEL SIZE:
9 x 9 microns

FOV:
1.5? x 1.0?. North = left, East = down

TEMPERATURE:
-30?

LUMINANCE:
16 x 1 minute (1x1 bin = 2.0"/pix)

RGB:
8 x 1 minute (2x2 bin = 4.0"/pix)

OTHER: H-A
-

OTHER:
-

OTHER:
-

PROCESSING:
Maxim DL, Photoshop

CONDITIONS:
Seeing = good, Transparency = Good
NOTES:
Ion tail pointing to SE

Cheers

John Drummond
Possum Observatory (IAU Code: E94)
Gisborne, New Zealand
E 177° 53', S 38° 38'
Email: john_drummond@xtra.co.nz
Website: http://www.possumobservatory.co.nz
Images: http://www.possumobservatory.co.nz/latest_images-all-continuing.htm

Date:  Sat, 31 May 2008 07:14:40 -0000
From:  algwat 
Subject:  Re: Comet Boattini (C/2007 W1) image from last night
--- In Comet-Images@yahoogroups.com, "J.P.Navarro Pina"
wrote:
>
> I imaged Comet Boattini (C/2007 W1) last night (30.29-34 May 2008
UT). I seemed to have picked up a 1? ion tail pointing in a PA of
125? (~SE). It was taken with a 20cm f4.6 Vixen Newtonian. The images
were median combined in Maxim DL and processed in Photoshop.
>
> IMAGING DATE: 30.29-34 May 2008 (UT)
>

Gidday All,

I have uploaded a movie of images from the SECCHI/STEREO solar
viewing satellite. They show a solar wind front passing over Boattini
W1. The images are two hours between frames, from 20080524-27. In
these images I see a short burst of materail leaving the comet,
moving fast left with the front on 20080527 around 0600hrs.

Recent images across this period, from Michael Mattiazzo and John
Drummond, show the comet had brightened and that an Ion tail had
developed. The comet may be in a higher density solar wind after the
front had passsed which is producing a more pronounced Ion tail.

Any other ground based images across this period would be interesting.

For you consideration, kind reagrds, Alan.

Date:  Sat, 07 Jun 2008 03:34:06 +1200
From:  John Drummond 
Subject:  Comet Image - Boattini, C/2007W1
Hi all,

I imaged Comet 2007 W1 (Boattini) on June 3.35-38 with a 20cm (8")@f4.6 Newtonian and SBIG STL11000M CCD. The ion tail that I had imaged on May 30 has seemingly all but disappeared. Exposure times were similar - in fact slightly more for June 3:
June 3 - 2 minute sublights, 9 x luminance (1x1), 5 x rgb (2x2), -30*C
May 30 - 1 minute sublights, 16 x luminance (1x1), 8 x rgb (2x2), -30*C

North is left and East down on both images. FOV = ~1.5d x 1.0d.

June 3 image -
http://www.possumobservatory.co.nz/comet_boatini--20cm@f4,6-2min-080603-9xlum1x1-5xrgb2x2.jpg
or
http://tinyurl.com/6my7am

May 30 image -
http://www.possumobservatory.co.nz/comet_2007W1-boatinni-20cm@f5,2-1min-16xlum-1x1_8xrgb-2x2-080530-0703-0815UT-drummond.jpg
or
http://tinyurl.com/4v7j7x

Cheers

John Drummond
Possum Observatory (IAU Code: E94)
Gisborne, New Zealand
E 177° 53', S 38° 38'
Email: john_drummond@xtra.co.nz
Website: http://www.possumobservatory.co.nz

Date:  Sun, 15 Jun 2008 16:12:48 +1000
From:  Michael Mattiazzo 
Subject:  C/2007 W1 Boattini images June 14 2008

Hi all,

I've uploaded images of comet C/2007 W1 Boattini taken last evening June 14
on my website.
It visually appears about magnitude 4.5-5 with a 15' coma but moonlight and
low elevation affect observation.

http://www.yp-connect.net/~mmatti/

2008 June 14.35UT.
Left: a stack of 3x1 minute exposures, Canon 300D digital camera.
200mm zoom lens, cropped image. ISO 800. East is up. FOV 1 degree wide.
Right: a stack of 3x1 minute exposures, Canon 300D digital camera.
100mm zoom lens, cropped image. ISO 800. East is up. FOV 3 degrees wide.
Delta Lepus (mag 3.9) is to the left of the comet.
Moonlight interference. Note the faint ion tail pointing towards Delta
Lepus.
Comet was at low elevation and heading into the morning sky.

Cheers,
Michael Mattiazzo
Castlemaine Victoria

Date:  Sun, 29 Jun 2008 14:33:29 +1200
From:  John Drummond 
Subject:  Comet Boattini (C/2007W1) photo from this morning
Hi all,

I imaged C/2007 W1 (Boattini) this morning (2008 June Saturday 28.70 UT) - it's currently rising about 4 hours before the Sun in the east for New Zealand. I've finally got myself a new focuser for the 16" (after a year) so that I can now get back into cometography - it's from Moonlite focusers and it works beautifully...

Boattini was imaged with my 16" (41cm) @ f5.2 Meade Newtonian and an SBIG STL11000M CCD. I took one minute sublights - 16 x lum (1x1), 8 x rgb (2x2), camera set to -30*C. I median combined it to help bring out the ion tail, but the stars are almost gone. North = down, East = right. FOV = ~0.9d x 0.6d - the tail is a little over 0.5 degrees in length. Slight moonlight/twilight interference.

http://www.possumobservatory.co.nz/c-2007w1-boattini--41cm@f5,2-16xlum1x1-8xrgb2x2-30c-080628-web2.jpg
or
http://tinyurl.com/6q7vpt

Cheers

John Drummond
Possum Observatory (IAU Code: E94)
Gisborne, New Zealand
E 177° 53', S 38° 38'
Email: john_drummond@xtra.co.nz
Website: http://www.possumobservatory.co.nz
Images: http://www.possumobservatory.co.nz/latest_images-all-continuing.htm

Date:  Sat, 05 Jul 2008 22:02:42 +1000
From:  Michael Mattiazzo 
Subject:  C/2007 W1 Boattini image July 4 2008
Hi all,

I've uploaded an image of comet C/2007 W1 Boattini taken this morning July
5th (July 4 UT)
on my website.

I observed it with the unaided eye at magnitude 5.2.
Through 25x100mm binoculars, the tail length is about 2 degrees and coma
diameter 15'.
The coma appears moderately condensed DC4/5.

Suffered frostbite for the effort.

http://www.yp-connect.net/~mmatti/

2008 July 04.82UT.
A stack of 3x2 minute exposures, Canon 300D digital camera.
200mm zoom lens, cropped image. ISO 800. FOV 4 degrees wide.

This will be my last image as I'm away on extended leave.

Cheers,
Michael 

Date:  Sun, 06 Jul 2008 15:54:09 +1200
From:  John Drummond 
Subject:  19P (Findlay) image from Thurs 3rd July
Hi all,

here's a link to an image of Comet 19P (Findlay) that I took on Thursday 3.70 July 2008.

Findlay was imaged with my 16" (41cm) @ f5.2 Meade Newtonian and an SBIG STL11000M CCD from a dark site. I took one minute sublights - 10 x lum (1x1), 5 x rgb (2x2), camera set to -30*C. Median combined. North = down, East = right. FOV = ~0.6d x 0.4d. I think that a tail/elongation may be seen extending in a PA of about 250˚(?).

See:
http://www.possumobservatory.co.nz/comet_15p-findlay-41cm@f5,2-10xlum1x1-5xrgb2x2-30c-080705-drummond-web.jpg
or
http://tinyurl.com/5casfs

Cheers

John Drummond
Possum Observatory (IAU Code: E94)
Gisborne, New Zealand
E 177° 53', S 38° 38'
Email: john_drummond@xtra.co.nz
Website: http://www.possumobservatory.co.nz
Images: http://www.possumobservatory.co.nz/latest_images-all-continuing.htm

Hi Mr. Muler :

What results scientifics obtained yours treatments and filters ....?

I do not understand multiaperture photometry ccd cometary ....? you have explain ?

Your writing Ang , is Alpha .... Alpha = 28.0 LS filter , be careful when interpreting the results obtained with this parameter a too large Alpha can produce false details , values from 1 to 20 degrees are suggested , you must be cautious LS filter .

Date:  Wed, 09 Jul 2008 14:48:45 -0000
From:  Dave Kodama 
Subject:  Discussions on this group
Please, everyone let's keep this public forum a civil place for
posting our comet images. While scientific discussions of the images
are also welcome, they need not degenerate to insults.

To those who have been insulted, please avoid replying publicly and
fanning the flames. The archived posts with insults will be deleted.

Those who persist in coloring their posts with insults will be placed
without discussion on moderated status (email will not be posted
automatically). Continuing to interfere with the posting of images
will get offenders ejected from the list. If you think you have been
wrongly removed, you can re-apply to get on the list if you include a
(calm) explanation of your side.

Thanks for your cooperation.

Date:  Sat, 12 Jul 2008 16:31:22 +0200
From:  Albert van Duin 
Subject:  (C/2006 OF2) Broughton image
Hello all,

Last night I made some images of (C/2006 OF2) Broughton, although the nights are still grey here at almost 53 degrees north.
10 x 3 minute sub exposures between 23:41 UT (July 11 2008) and 0:13 UT from Beilen, the Netherlands using my 20cm F/2.75 ASA Astrograph and modified Canon 40D at 800 ISO.

http://astropix.nl/images/2006OF2/2006OF2-CombineFilesAdpAdd-crop100.jpg

It is a full size crop from the image which included Messier 34.
The smudge to the right (south) of the comet is galaxy PGC 10079, magnitude 15.2.

The sub exposures were unguided, using the 10Micron GM2000-QCI mount in "Follow Object" mode.

Regards,
Albert van Duin

http://www.astropix.nl

Date:  Sat, 26 Jul 2008 12:58:31 +1200
From:  John Drummond 
Subject:  Image - C/2007G1 (LINEAR)
Hi all,

I did some astrometry of C/2007G1 (LINEAR) last night and decided to stack the 20 x 1 minute 1000x1000 pixel luminance images together. A tail can be seen extending for about 4' to the NE. Image details are below (I hope the lined chart doesn't get jumbled)...

http://www.possumobservatory.co.nz/C-2007g1-linear-41cm@f5,2-20x1min-Lum-1x1-25c-080725-1000x1000-med-web.jpg
or
http://tinyurl.com/58ekxr

Please forgive the mess below if my chart of imaging details gets jumbled...

IMAGING DETAILS -

TARGET:
C/2007G1 (LINEAR)

POSITION:
~ RA 15h 44m, Dec -31˚ 59'

MAG and SIZE:
Mag = ~11.5, Diameter = ~1'

IMAGING DATE: Friday 25.37-41 July 2008 (UT)

TELESCOPE:
41cm (16") Meade Newtonian

FOCAL LENGTH:
2132mm (@f5.2)

CAMERA:
SBIG STL11000M CCD

CHIP:
4008 x 2672 pixels (full 35mm)

PIXEL SIZE:
9 x 9 microns

FOV:
~12'x 12' (cropped). North=up, East=left

TEMPERATURE:
-25˚

LUMINANCE:
20 x 1 minute (1x1 binning)

RGB:
-

OTHER: H-A
-

OTHER:
-

OTHER:
-

PROCESSING:
Maxim DL, Photoshop

CONDITIONS:
Seeing = Fair, Transparency = Poor
NOTES:
Images used for astrometry

Cheers

John Drummond

Danilo,

I adjusted your photo of C/2008 J1 with Photoshop and found dust
trail-like feature:
http://s47.radikal.ru/i116/0807/37/c32e348151eb.jpg

I speculate that such elliptic coma and possible dust trail are formed
by heavy meteoroid-like particles. Sometimes dust trails become
anti-tails (in case of C/1956 R1 (Arend-Roland) such dust trail was
VERY strong).

Kind regards,
Dimitry

Date:  Sat, 26 Jul 2008 19:39:48 -0000
From:  Dimitry Chestnov

Hello Giovanni and all,

This feature is very thin, straight and long, unlikely to be dust
tail. Now heliocentric distance is around 1.7 AU, so it is unlikely to
be ion tail (and direction of "feature" is rather different from
anti-solar direction). The position angle of this possible dust trail
coincide with orbit direction (checked in Celestia):
http://s61.radikal.ru/i173/0807/60/a9fe22982255.png

I also checked another images of this comet and found something in
Michael Jaeger's image (north is below):

original:http://kometen.fg-vds.de/pix/2008J1/2008J1_24062008.htm
adjusted: http://s48.radikal.ru/i122/0807/98/8b0e6f3d6dad.jpg

Vitali Nevski (Vitebsk, Belarus) also reports about sunward feature.

Best regards,
Dimitry 

Date:  Sat, 26 Jul 2008 22:22:00 +0200
From:  "gvnn64\@libero\.it" 
Subject:  Re:[Comet-Images] Re: Possible dust trail of C/2008 J1 (Boattini)
As far as I know, cometary trails are only observed on short period comets, since they are the "memory" of previous perihelion passages. According the MPC website, C/2008 J1 (Boattini) has an eccentricity of about 0.99, i.e. extremely long period (if periodic at all).

Under these circumstances, a trail would be very unstable, and unlikely to survive to the following perihelion passage.

So, unless the orbital elements of this comet will change significantly, I suspect that a trail on C/2008 J1 would be rather ulikely...

Cheers,
Giovanni

Date:  Mon, 28 Jul 2008 04:30:33 -0000
From:  Dennis Persyk 
Subject:  C/2007 N3 Lunin
It has a relative motion of 2.36 arc seconds per minute so I was
limited to 120 second exposures when I imaged it to avoid blur.

Conditions were exceedingly poor in north central Illinois on the
morning of July 27. The comet was only 27 degrees high and I could
see no stars at all in the area. The only thing I saw in the area by
unaided eye was Jupiter, and I saw one magnitude 7 star through my 4-
inch refractor.

I was amazed that the Epsilon 160 f/3.3 astrograph and SXV-H9 camera
could pick out details from the murk.

Images, associated data, and imaging notes at
http://home.att.net/~dpersyk/new.htm

Please take a look and give me some feedback. This was quite an
imaging challenge for me. Thank you for visiting my site.

Clear skies,

Dennis Persyk
Igloo Observatory Home Page http://dpersyk.home.att.net
Hampshire, IL

Pier Design Paper: http://home.att.net/~dpersyk/Pier_Design.htm

From:  Erik Bryssinck 
Subject:  Image of 199P of 04 and 06 aug.
Hello,

Here the image of comet 199P of 6 august:

http://www.astronomie.be/erik.bryssinck/menu.html

CCD-magnetude without filter: 14.4 in window of 24 arc. sec (this is the
very small coma that can be noticed with software enhancement technics)
comet is starlike object.

image of 4 august:

http://www.astronomie.be/erik.bryssinck/199P_shoemaker.html

Date:  Wed, 06 Aug 2008 13:29:11 +0200
From:  Jose Pablo Navarro Pina 
Subject:  image 199p/
Hi all ,

Image ccd of comet 199p/ , the photometry calculated by SYPHORA ( System Photometric of Radius Aperture ) , is m1 ( A.R. 3 pix. ) = +14.8 +/- 0.1 ( filter R , USNO B1 ) .
The analysis of PBS is ADU max = 3.700 , ADU min 3.450 , A.R.=3 pix. , diameter ( d ) = 11 arcsec .

Image here :

http://webs.ono.com/jpab

J.P.Navarro Pina
Observatorio Astronomico "Vega del Thader"
MPC-J70 , Spain.
Project SYPHORA .

Date:  Thu, 07 Aug 2008 22:11:26 +0100
From:  gus muler telefónica 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] 199p shoemaker 06-08-2008
Thank you very much Charles.!
Sometimes I am not sure if posting CCD links here, cos I can see a lot more of visual observings.
Makes me happy to see your interest.
I find it more than interesting and full of information like a comets list, and for sure, makes me feel proud to post here.
well, let´s come back home...
for this graph, I hope it was worthy and well used, I mixed the BRI and Luminance with the LRGB combination in the Maxim.
with the same program, wich I found marvellous, in VIEW and LINE PROFILE WINDOW.
they are many different sistems to measure there, like lineal horizontal histogr. plot frame, etc.
as well, the astroart makes it very easy.

As you know, I don´t know a lot about photometry, I am just a neophyte in all this cuestions, but the sensor is more sensitive to the red, is ST8 xme.
I have this filters for less than a month, but looks very interestin in this comets field.
I´ll do triyngs with filters measuring separately, and then compare with this one, so, we can know how this representation.
aplicable to the photometry, .

when I improved, I did not realize this matters.

very bad seiing today, sirocco in canary islands. let´s see if we have a picture from today.

regards, gustavo.

The summer seeing where I am, has limited me.
I have been imaging 6P and C/2007 N3 with lots more frames hoping to see any developing structure. The coma on C/2007 N3 seems to be elongating a little toward the East (PA 090)  in my image stacks.
http://cometskies.com/images/C2007N3-08022008-0533UT.jpg
I appreciate seeing the "CCD" discussions on this group. I too am not a "visual" comet observer. It seems there are always plenty of CCD targets each night I can get out and I never have enough time to switch setups.
Best wishes to you,
CharlesC. Bell H47 Vicksburg
http://cometskies.com

Date:  Thu, 07 Aug 2008 15:03:43 -0700
From:  Charles Bell 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] 199p shoemaker 06-08-2008
I don't understand what L+I-RVB actually means.
I would think that one would want to compare images in each bandpass, B, V, R, and I etc. possibly trying to account for the difference in sensor quantum efficiency by perhaps stacking more B frames than R frames etc  since the ST-8XME sensor is more efficient in R. This is just a thought.
There are probably others around here that could make some suggestions.
It has been put forth in discussions that CO or carbon monoxide emissions provides much of the blue.
Is water vapor emission stronger in I?
These two comets, 6P and C/2007 N3 are pretty bright and well placed for observing for several months. 6P reaches perihelion next week and is already slowly decreasing in magnitude.
C/2007 N3 is slowly brightening. It might make a good study to compare the two. Again, just thinking out loud here.

 C. Bell H47 Vicksburg
http://cometskies.com

Date:  Fri, 08 Aug 2008 07:24:29 -0000
From:  gvnn64 
Subject:  Re: 199p shoemaker 06-08-2008
> I was curious if you could determine if any particular comet is
brighter in B, V, R or I, etc.

Yes, you can do it, but not looking straight away at the images: you
must perform some photometry, measuring the flux of the comet and
some refence stars in several apertures and passbands

> I would think that one would want to compare images in each
bandpass, B, V, R, and I etc. possibly trying to account for the
difference in sensor quantum efficiency by perhaps stacking more B
frames than R frames etc  since the ST-8XME sensor is more efficient
in R. This is just a thought.

Well, this can be done as a first glance, however it's a very rough
method, and the results might be misleading. The best approach is the
analytical procedure I mentioned above.

> It has been put forth in discussions that CO or carbon monoxide
emissions provides much of the blue.

This is correct.

> Is water vapor emission stronger in I?

Ionized water (H2O+) is mainly emitting in the red (@620nm); some
emissions might also be present in the I band, but much less obvious
compared to the R band.

> These two comets, 6P and C/2007 N3 are pretty bright and well
placed for observing for several months. 6P reaches perihelion next
week and is already slowly decreasing in magnitude.
> C/2007 N3 is slowly brightening. It might make a good study to
compare the two.

It might be instructive: these two comets are showing a very
different behaviour, and they are characterize by striking orbital
differences; 6P/d'Arrest is a typical short period, Jupiter-family
comet, rather rich in gas. C/2007 N3 (Lulin) is rapresentative of the
Oort-cloud comets, with a parabolic retrograde orbit, and it appears
rich in dust.

Cheers,
Giovanni Sostero

http://remanzacco.blogspot.com/
http://www.cara-project.org

> > These two comets, 6P and C/2007 N3 are pretty bright and well
> placed for observing for several months. 6P reaches perihelion next
> week and is already slowly decreasing in magnitude.
> > C/2007 N3 is slowly brightening. It might make a good study to
> compare the two.
>
> It might be instructive: these two comets are showing a very
> different behaviour, and they are characterize by striking orbital
> differences; 6P/d'Arrest is a typical short period, Jupiter-family
> comet, rather rich in gas. C/2007 N3 (Lulin) is rapresentative of the
> Oort-cloud comets, with a parabolic retrograde orbit, and it appears
> rich in dust.
>
> Cheers,
> Giovanni Sostero
>
> http://remanzacco.blogspot.com/
> http://www.cara-project.org
> 

Date:  Fri, 08 Aug 2008 17:21:59 +0200
From:  Wolfgang Renz 
Subject:  [Comet-Images] Re: 199p shoemaker 06-08-2008
Hello

> I was curious if you could determine if any particular comet is
> brighter in B, V, R or I, etc.

If one looks at the image and its ADU values directly, the impression
will depend of course on the QE of the CCD, transmission of the
atmosphere (extinction), scope and filter and of course on the emis-
sion of the comet in the different bands.

With simple aperture photometry one can easily determine mag
values in the different bands. But as a comet is usually not a point
source, the results will strongly depend on the choosen aperture
diameter. Here a standardization is required to make the results
comparable and useful at all (see FOCAS, CARA AfRho, ...).
I can send a post on comet photometry that I prepaped for an other
group some time ago if somebody is interested in it.

If a comet is producing just dust (like 17P Holmes), it will show
a continuum spectrum of mainly reflected sunlight. Therefore it
should look whitish beige if the image is well calibrated.

If the comet is producing lots of gas, it will show a broad emission
line spectrum with the dominating CN line ~ 380-390 nm (U band
and a bit B band) and the major C2 lines at ~ 495-530 nm (V band
and a bit B band) and ~ 455-475 nm (B band) and ~ 540-565 nm
(V band and a bit Rc band) with a more or less strong continuum
due to dust. Therefore it should look bluish green if the image is
well calibrated.

Clear skies
Wolfgang

--
Wolfgang Renz, Karlsruhe, Germany
Rz.BAV = WRe.vsnet = RWG.AAVSO

----- Original Message -----
From: "gvnn64"
To:
Sent: Friday, August 08, 2008 9:24 AM
Subject: [Comet-Images] Re: 199p shoemaker 06-08-2008

> I was curious if you could determine if any particular comet is
> brighter in B, V, R or I, etc.

Yes, you can do it, but not looking straight away at the images: you
must perform some photometry, measuring the flux of the comet and
some refence stars in several apertures and passbands

> I would think that one would want to compare images in each
bandpass, B, V, R, and I etc. possibly trying to account for the
difference in sensor quantum efficiency by perhaps stacking more B
frames than R frames etc since the ST-8XME sensor is more efficient
in R. This is just a thought.

Well, this can be done as a first glance, however it's a very rough
method, and the results might be misleading. The best approach is the
analytical procedure I mentioned above.

> It has been put forth in discussions that CO or carbon monoxide
emissions provides much of the blue.

This is correct.

> Is water vapor emission stronger in I?

Ionized water (H2O+) is mainly emitting in the red (@620nm); some
emissions might also be present in the I band, but much less obvious
compared to the R band.

> These two comets, 6P and C/2007 N3 are pretty bright and well
placed for observing for several months. 6P reaches perihelion next
week and is already slowly decreasing in magnitude.
> C/2007 N3 is slowly brightening. It might make a good study to
compare the two.

It might be instructive: these two comets are showing a very
different behaviour, and they are characterize by striking orbital
differences; 6P/d'Arrest is a typical short period, Jupiter-family
comet, rather rich in gas. C/2007 N3 (Lulin) is rapresentative of the
Oort-cloud comets, with a parabolic retrograde orbit, and it appears
rich in dust.

Cheers,
Giovanni Sostero

http://remanzacco.blogspot.com/
http://www.cara-project.org

------------------------------------

Subject:  Comet Imagers
Hello
I have been running the same thought through my mind for some time
now. I would really like to see a gathering of comet imagers from
around the world. This could take a couple of years or more but it
could happen with input from all and good plans or perhaps there is
already a meeting planned that I don't know about. I'm not really
talking about the science of comets but putting them on the chip in
ways that would be good enough for the science to use or adjusted to
use in the best publications. There are so few true comet imagers
that I consider us special with the ability to learn from each
other. Perhaps we could meet at an observatory with time rented
while there or travel to a remote area with good skys and bring our
own equipment. There are some really good things that could come
from this and ideas are what I am after for now. I would ask the
members to give this some though and contact me in private with your
thoughts. Remember this could be planned around an upcomming comet
event or a weather factor that will give the best chance for good
skys. I for one would love to meet in person other imagers and learn
from your expert knowledge. Who knows, we might even get some
press. We are a small, special group with a skill for imaging an
oject like no other. How about giving this some thought and let me
know if your interested. Contact me at tricks46@yahoo.com
Mike H.

From:  jdilapo 
Subject:  Re: 2008 A1 McNaught, 6P d'Arrest, 22 Aug 08
Hi Rob,

I'm a new member and I've done my share of comet imaging over the
years. Comet 6P d'Arrest looked like an interesting target to image
after seeing your shot. I've been wanting to try out some image
processing techniques for comets ... so, I got a shot in last night
(8/23) while waiting for my main target to rise higher in the sky. Not
the best comet to shoot, since it was only about 20 degrees above the
horizon, but I'm pleased with the new processing. The image is
available at:

http://www.geocities.com/jdilapo/Comet_6P_dArrest.jpg

Jim

Date:  Mon, 25 Aug 2008 03:15:28 -0000
From:  jdilapo 
Subject:  Re: 2008 A1 McNaught, 6P d'Arrest, 22 Aug 08
Hey Rick,

I wanted to try out the special comet stacking routine in "Deep Sky
Stacker". You can stack on the stars, stack on the comet or combine
the two to produce a stationary comet image on a fixed starry
background. I've done this manually, but it's a real processing
"pain". It's nice to have it all done automatically! Give it a try.
BTW, after taking a closer look at my original image, I noticed
quite an extended, faint coma surrounding d'Arrest. I re-processed the
image to bring out this faint detail and comet now looks pretty
spectacular. The coma extends out over 4 arc minutes. Here's the link:

http://www.geocities.com/jdilapo/Comet_6P_dArrest_30m.jpg

Jim

From:  Michael Mattiazzo 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] Images of comets 6P,  C/2006 OF2, C/2007 W1
Hello all,

Note that Earth has been crossing the orbit of comet Boattini C/2007 W1 this past week.
You can just see a faint "anti-tail" pointing in the direction opposite to the main tail.
With a bit of image processing, you can see it better.

Nice images,
Cheers,
Michael Mattiazzo

Subject: Re: [Comet-Images] Images of comets 6P, C/2006 OF2, C/2007 W1

Hello all,

Note that Earth has been crossing the orbit of comet Boattini C/2007 W1 this past week.
You can just see a faint "anti-tail" pointing in the direction opposite to the main tail.
With a bit of image processing, you can see it better.

Nice images,
Cheers,
Michael Mattiazzo

Date:  Sun, 31 Aug 2008 10:01:01 -0000
From:  Korotkiy Stanislav 
Subject:  Possible supernova near C/2005 L3 (McNaught)!
Dear Sirs!

Yesterday, we discovery possible supernova (mag approximately 19.2)
near by C/2005 L3 (McNaught)! 19' S-E from comet!

Please, confirmed possible supernova!

Discovery new supernova in UGC 09578 (PGC 053239)
-----------------------------------------------------------------

S. Korotkiy (Ka-Dar obs., Moscow), T. Kryachko and B.Satovskiy
(Astrotel obs., KSU) report the discovery of an apparent supernova
(mag approximately 19.2) on the five a unfiltered images with
exposition 300 sec (lim mag 21.0) taken on Aug. 30.72 UT with the
Takahashi FRC-300 (D=300mm, F=2330mm) + CCD Apogee Alta U9000 at
Kazan State University Astrotel observatory (Karachay-Cherkessia,
Russia, MPCCOD: 114). The new object is located at R.A. = 14h 53m
48s.26 +/- 0".1, Decl. = +20d 06' 45".5 +/- 0".1 (equinox 2000.0),
which is about 23".1 east and 12".1 south of the center of the galaxy
UGC 09578 (PGC 053239). Nothing is visible at this position on a
Palomar Sky Survey (POSS-II Blue) obtained 1993-05-19 06:28:00 (via
the Digitized Sky Survey; limiting mag 21.5). In MPChecker no
asteroids.

Discovery image:


DSS plate (obtained 1993-05-19 06:28:00):

Date:  Mon, 08 Sep 2008 04:20:20 -0000
From:  Rob 
Subject:  Tails on C/2008 A1 McNaught?
Hi all! A1 is low at dusk in our southern skies and moonlight is
increasing. I haven't seen too many recent photos of A1, but some of
the latest show tails.

I have severe limitations with my imaging equipment (hand guiding,
ricketty mount), but I captured this image last night. I put together
a composite, and without wanting to draw too many conclusions from
poor data, it appears to show a couple of interesting features.

http://robsastropics.googlepages.com/A17Sept08comp.jpg

The shot on the left is a widefield showing A1 in very interesting
territory and on the 9th it will be just 3 degrees from the galaxy
Centaurus A. The stack of seven subs was on the stars, so the head
of the comet (lower-left) is smeared. But it shows the faintest
trace of a tail extending for about a degree, up between two stars to
its upper left.

The images on the right are from a stack of seven resized crops,
stacked on the comet head and with the comet at centre. The tail
showing in the LH shot is very diffuse and faint. But beside it is a
distinct, very thin straight line extending out more than a degree,
at about 45 deg from horizontal and towards upper left.

I'd be very interested to know if anyone has managed to image this
comet with better equipment (and processing, LOL), and can maybe
confirm these features (long narrow diffuse dust trail & long thin
ion trail??). Thanks!

Cheers -

Rob

Date:  Tue, 09 Sep 2008 20:42:39 +1000
From:  Michael Mattiazzo 
Subject:  C/2008 A1 McNaught image Sep 2
Hello all,

My comets website has been offline for the past week but is now back online.
I've uploaded an image of comet C/2008 A1 McNaught taken last week,

2008 Sep 02.45UT.
A stack of 3x2 minute exposures, Canon 300D digital camera.
300mm zoom lens, cropped image. ISO 800.

http://www.yp-connect.net/~mmatti/

My visual observation of the comet that evening,
2008 Sep 2.44UT: m1=6.6, Dia.=7', DC=6...10x50mm B...Michael Mattiazzo
(Castlemaine, Victoria)

Plus theres another eclipse pic, if you haven't yet already seen it.
Canon 300D digital camera and 300mm zoom lens cropped. ISO 100.
combined 2x1 second exposures. Unsharp mask processing. Note the intricate
detail in the coronal filaments, marking the magnetic field lines of the
Sun. You can also see subtle detail on the lunar surface. The Magnitude 4.0
star delta Cancri can be seen to the lower right.

Cheers.

Date:  Mon, 22 Sep 2008 20:27:52 -0500
From:  "Dr. D. T. Durig" 
Subject:  RE: [Comet-Images] 205P/Giacobini September 22, 2008  0314UT
I stacked pretty deep and dirty to get the fragments, between 20 and 60
minutes exposure per each frame in the stacks. For those that want to see
what I saw the animations are here:

http://arthur.sewanee.edu/obsv/view.php

This reminds me a lot of what I saw in the fragments of 73P, just not spread
out as far. In the frames from 9/22 it almost appears that there is a
continuous line of faint debris from the parent body to the more distant
fragment 10 arc minutes to the west. I am searching further west tonight,
looking for more faint fragments.

Dr. D. T. Durig

Cordell-Lorenz Observatory

The University of the South

Sewanee TN

ddurig@sewanee.edu

OBS CODE 850

From:  John Drummond 
Subject:  Image - Comet McNaught (C/2008A1)
Hi all,

here's an image of Comet McNaught (C/2008A1) taken last night (Sunday 28.33-35 Sept - UT). 41cm scope @ f4.6 with a modified Canon 350D @ 800 ISO. 20 x 1 minute. Note the tail extending for at least 26' in a PA of 114.

Hi all,

here's an image of Comet McNaught (C/2008A1) taken last night (Sunday 28.33-35 Sept - UT). 41cm scope @ f4.6 with a modified Canon 350D @ 800 ISO. 20 x 1 minute. Note the tail extending for at least 26' in a PA of 114.

Date:  Wed, 01 Oct 2008 09:55:36 +1300
From:  John Drummond 
Subject:  Close approach - 144P/Pleiades/Hertha
Hi all,

it looks like there could be an interesting photo/visual opportunity on about October 26-28 when comet 144P (P/Kushida - mag 13?) lies about 3.5 degrees WSW of M45 (Pleiades) and about 6' south of asteroid 135 (Hertha - mag 11.2?).

Cheers

John Drummond

From:  tricks46

The skys were clear although it was a little windy after a cold
front passage. After taking longer exposures I returned to reduce
the time to 20 second exposures. Stacking was done with ccdsoftv5
and this image is the end result. I don't know and cannot say if
the comet is comming totally apart or not although it appears so
according to this image. Hope others can show reduced time
exposures to possible show comet progress.

Date:  Thu, 02 Oct 2008 09:58:34 +1300
From:  John Drummond 
Subject:  C/2008A1 (McNaught) image - ~1 degree tail
Hi all,

I imaged Comet McNaught (C/2008A1) again last night (Oct 1.31-39) but with a shorter focal length to try and pick up more of the tail. I used a 20cm (8") Vixen Newtonian at f4.6 with a modified Canon 350D @ 800asa. 34 x 2.5 minute subs were used. The tail is seen extending in a PA of 110° (ESE) for nearly 1 degree. North is up, east is left in this cropped image (~1.5°x 1°).

Comet McNaught is currently in the evening sky in the WSW from New Zealand - about 30 degrees in altitude and about 15 degrees west of Antares. It is heading roughly NE at just over a degree a day...

http://www.possumobservatory.co.nz/comet_2008a1-mcnaught-20cm@f4,6-350d-34x2,5mins-081001-drummond-web.jpg
or
http://tinyurl.com/5476nc

Cheers

John Drummond
Possum Observatory (IAU Code: E94)
Gisborne, New Zealand
E 177° 53', S 38° 38'
Email: john_drummond@xtra.co.nz
Website: http://www.possumobservatory.co.nz
Images: http://www.possumobservatory.co.nz/latest_images-all-continuing.htm

Date:  Thu, 02 Oct 2008 17:53:10 -0000
From:  chergen 
Subject:  Comet Images - 29P - 205P - C/2007 W1 - P/2008 L2 - P/2008 Q2
Greetings everyone,

I have posted a number of comet images taken with the University
of Arizona's Kuiper 1.54-m on 2008 Sept 29.

The images can be found on my blog at

http://transientsky.wordpress.com

And more specifically at this post

http://transientsky.wordpress.com/2008/10/02/comet-observations-sept-29/

205P-A is still going strong. 205P-B looks faint and diffuse is
~6 magnitudes fainter than 205P-A. I was not able to find 205P-C.

Processed images of the latest outburst 29P show similar
structures to what was seen last year with Comet Holmes.

Regards,
Carl Hergenrother

Date:  Mon, 06 Oct 2008 09:19:27 -0000
From:  Freddy WILLEMS 
Subject:  Comet 2008 A1 McNaught - another try........

Different exposure times, from 10 s., 15 s., 30 s., 40 s. and 50 s. ISO
400 and 800 settings.

Meade 14" LX200 UHTC - Canon 10 D focal reducer 6.3

The sky is to bright for longer exposures and there is not much time to
image the comet in the twilight.

Have a lot of light polution in the W ! (Tennis Courts),

Stack of 24 images with different exposure times to 'beat' the light
polution.

Earlier I tried to image 2008 A1 with the WO 102 f/7 and Canon 10D focal
reducer 6.3, but that was not a great Idea, the WO is really a light
'grabber', images were to bright to bring the comet out.

Need darker skies ! [B-)]

Stack on Comet:

http://tech.ph.groups.yahoo.com/group/Comet-Images/photos/view/948c?b=2&\
m=f&o=0
&m=f&o=0>

Stack on stars:

http://tech.ph.groups.yahoo.com/group/Comet-Images/photos/view/948c?b=1&\
m=f&o=0
&m=f&o=0>

Freddy

Can someone please tell what is the current observed magnitude of
this comet? The last observed magnitude in 'Astrosite Groningen'
lists it to be 14th mag in early September. The tail REALLY seems
pretty impressive for a 14th mag comet!

What would be its current distance? 'Aerith.net' lists its q = 1.68
AU and perihelion in 2008 June. Has this now crossed Mars orbit, or
is it intrinsically faint?

Not able to generate the Orbit Diagram for it at:

http://ssd.jpl.nasa.gov/sbdb.cgi?ID=c00051_0

PS - There seems to be a fragment of this too, by the name 51/P-A.

Date:  Tue, 14 Oct 2008 18:42:19 +0200
From:  Juan Jose Gonzalez Suarez 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] 51P/Harrington.
Amar,

My last visual estimate ( published in Astrosite Groningen ) was:

51P/Harrington:
2008 Sep. 7.15 UT: m1=14.0, Dia.=0.3', DC=5, 20 cm SCT (160x).
[ Nearby field stars checked in DSS. Comparison stars taken from
Henden photometry near IK Tau. Mountain location, very clear sky ].
( Leon, N. Spain )

Near the same date, multiaperture CCD photometry ( R-band ) from MPC 232
( Esteban Reina, Observatorio Masquefa, Barcelona ) was:

OBJECT DATE UT 10"x10" 20x20 30x30 40x40 50x50
60"x60"
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------
51P 06/Sep/2008 02:39:31 15.89 15.31 15.04 14.83 14.74
14.71

Furtherly, in Sep.29th, Mount Lemmon (MPC G96) CCD photometry was ~14.0
(T), ( MPEC T99 ).

I don't know any 51P' recent visual estimate, but CCD photometry (
R-band ) from MPC J47 ( Gustavo Muler, Observatorio Nazaret, Islas
Canarias ) on Oct.10th was:

OBJECT DATE UT 10"x10" 20x20 30x30 40x40 50x50
60"x60"
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------
51P 10/Oct/2008 01:54:04 16.94 15.93 15.39 15.03 14.73
14.47

( Image in
http://astrosurf.com/nazaret/images/cometas/51/51-081010-J47.jpg ;
tail length ~ 2' ; the brighter star just near the comet is GSC
1284-0058, mag. 14.7, )

[ MPC 232 and J47 CCD data from Cometas_Obs,
http://astrosurf.com/cometas-obs/index_i.htm ].

We can't compare directly CCD and visual photometry, but from the
previous data we can guess that the total visual magnitude m1 is now
around 14.0-14.5.

( Weather permitting, I'll try 51P visually again from the Cantabrian
Mountains in the next moonless period ).

Best regards and clear skies,

J. J. Gonzalez

P.S.: 51P is now at delta = 1.26 AU, r = 2.02 AU; intrinsically faint
with H=10.
You cand find an orbit diagram at :
http://www.perihelio.org/51porb.htm

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Date:  Tue, 14 Oct 2008 09:43:09 -0700
From:  Charles Bell 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] Re: 51P Harrington   2008 10 11
Enter 51P at
http://www.cfa.harvard.edu/iau/MPEph/MPEph.html
and hit the return or submit
and you will get an ephemeris with all the info you desire.

Date and submitted magnitude (if not blank) of last astrometric observation for each comet is at:
http://www.cfa.harvard.edu/iau/lists/LastCometObs.html

Recent comet magnitude estimates are posted at:
http://www.cfa.harvard.edu/icq/CometMags.html

Date:  Wed, 22 Oct 2008 09:38:01 -0000
From:  Freddy WILLEMS 
Subject:  Comet 2008 A1 McNaught -  Still no tail

I captured another 40 frames of C2008 A1 yesterday Oct. 20, 2008,

The exposures were only 20sec. ISO 800

Canon 10D unmodded - Focel reducer 6.3

Meade 14" LX200 UHTC GPS

Stacked in IP, curves and levels in PS.

Could not bring out any tail, will wait another week or so for another
try when the comet is higher in the sky

and in darker skies, so I can take longer exposure times. I have to much
LP in the W.

See different stacks,

http://tech.ph.groups.yahoo.com/group/Comet-Images/photos/view/948c?b=3&\
m=f&o=0
&m=f&o=0>

http://tech.ph.groups.yahoo.com/group/Comet-Images/photos/view/948c?b=4&\
m=f&o=0
&m=f&o=0>

Date:  Sun, 02 Nov 2008 18:13:48 -0000
From:  Bernhard Häusler 
Subject:  C/2008 T2 (Cardinal) meets PGC24802, 2008-11-01 UT17:23 LRGB , total 150min
Hi comet friends, I am new here, but not new in taking comet images.
Since 1998 I love to photograph comets with my ST8 and later with my
ST10XME. I am a member of the German comet group and some of you may
know me from my comet project between 1998 and 2001. Here is my newest
shot: C/2008 T2 (Cardinal), total 150 min. exp., 2008-11-01 UT17:23 to
UT 20:31, 12" SCT + ST10XME, Stars: RGB 3x30min., Comet: LRGB L=60min.,
RGB=30min. each, Lum.weight=10%, RGB scale = 1:2.5:6, Position of the
comet: UT19:30, 16.5 mag, tail: PA234°, image size: 11'*6'

http://www.amication.de/comets/c2008t2_20081101_txt.jpg

The galaxy PGC24802 has a suprisingly irregular shape, which you can't
see in TheSky.

Clear skies
Bernhard

Date:  Wed, 12 Nov 2008 21:25:40 -0000
From:  Bernhard Häusler 
Subject:  Quicktime Movie of C/2008 T2 (Cardinal) from 2008-11-08 - passing IC 512
Friends,

here a movie of the comet. You need the newest QuickTime Player of Apple.
The tail is remarkable distinctive under dark conditions, so turn off
your lights. The comet is moving almost northwards with 0.43" per
minute. The movie contains 14 images, 3 minutes exposure time each.
Unfortuately I had to stop the sequence, because the skies became cloudy.

http://www.amication.de/comets/comb14.mov

If you like, compare the movie with my images of the same day.

Enjoy and clear skies

Bernhard

Date:  Fri, 14 Nov 2008 17:17:19 -0000
From:  Bernhard Häusler 
Subject:  Re: Quicktime Movie of C/2008 T2 (Cardinal) from 2008-11-08 - passing IC 512
Hi Charles,

yes, the comet passed by IC512 and other faint galaxies at this day.
Here is the link in the forum.

http://tech.groups.yahoo.com/group/Comet-Images/message/4812

If a galaxy is good enough on the image, I always search for
supernovas by comparing the image with files from the Integrated
Image and Catalogue Archive Service of the USNO Flagstaff Station:
http://www.nofs.navy.mil/data/fchpix/
They send the desired images and then I compare the stars. The galaxy
of my video has no actual supernova.

In addition I am always searching for other moving objects on my
images, also doing photometry and astrometry.

I like your homepage and your telescope!

Clear skies

Bernhard

Date:  Fri, 14 Nov 2008 17:37:51 -0000
From:  Bernhard Häusler 
Subject:  C/2008 J1 (Boattini) from 2008-11-13 UT16:55 under full moon conditions
Hi all,

the full moon is really a challenge when taking comet images. But I
find out, that under such conditions you only need very long exposure
times for getting partly good images.
The magnitude limit of this image (~19 mag) is almost the same as on
other images taken without moon light.

http://www.amication.de/comets/c2008J1_20081113_txt.jpg

The shape has changed a bit since the last 2 months after the comet's
passage of the North Pole.

Clear skies

Bernhard

Date:  Sun, 16 Nov 2008 19:46:39 -0000
From:  Bernhard Häusler 
Subject:  Another movie night for comet C/2008 T2 (Cardinal)
Hi all,

I produced a movie from my images of C/2008 T2 (cardinal) from 2008-
11-07 UT17:13 to UT20:36.
The comet is moving NNE with 0.43" per minute. The 3 hours trail of
the comet is reduced to 6 seconds movie time.
It passed a distance of 1'18" in 180 minutes at this day. The Sun
distance is 3.20AU, the tail is 26" in PA289°.
The comet's current CCD magnitude of 16.4 will increase soon and it
will become a very good object for both observers and photographers
in the first quarter of 2009.
The size of the Quicktime Movie is 6504KB and best downloaded with
fast internet speed.
For watching the movie I recommend full screen watching in dark rooms.
See also message# 4823 in this forum for comparing the images.

http://www.amication.de/comets/c2008t2_20081107_video60.mov

Enjoy and have clear skies

Bernhard

Date:  Sat, 22 Nov 2008 22:09:36 -0000
From:  Piotr Guzik 
Subject:  Re: 85p
Mike, James, Clay,

> but still nothing within an 11 arc minute

The comet wasn't observed for more than 20 years. I think even 11' is
definitely not enough. If the comet is only 1 day late, it would me
about 35' from ephemeris position...
I think it would me much better to look for it even a few degrees
around ephemeris position (or rather along line of variation) with
limiting magnitude let's say 15-16 mag, than to look a few arc minutes
around that position but down to 20 mag.
If the comet still exists and is close to its expected position it
would have been found last year...

Best Regards
Piotr Guzik 

Date:  Sun, 23 Nov 2008 11:23:25 +1100
From:  Alan Watson 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] Re: 85p
Gidday All,
I have been searching in the STEREO-A HI2 images for this comet also. By my reckoning it should be square in the middle of the current Field of view which is approx 120 degrees. While the resolution is not good. Currently in the FOV I can detect D'arest, Neptune, and a couple of asteroids close by Neptune. Generally this imager can detect non fuzzy object down to about mag 11.5, and fuzzy's like D'arest down to about mag 10. It does see further into the infrared, and could detect Holmes all the way across its field FOV.

This all said, I am just confirming that as of now there is no Mag 10 or better object moving across the FOV in the line I am expecting Boethin to take. I can put up a small movie around Neptune that covers a good number of degrees , if you are interested.

In December I expect Boethin to be crossing the HI-1 imager, which has a FOV of approx 20 degrees and can see down to Mag 14.

Oh, It is passing much closer behind the STEREO B imagers so will not be detectable unless they roll the space craft, not a likly event.

Kind regards,
Alan Watson

Http://cometal.bigblog.com.au/index.do

Date:  Sun, 23 Nov 2008 19:43:40 -0000
From:  tricks46 
Subject:  Re: 85p
Hello. Well I spent friday night for about 3 hours imaging the area
of and 2 degrees all around where the comet was to be. I used a
35mm 135mm lense connected to the ST10xmei. I couldn't locate any
comet with B/W or color information, although I did see some small
spots that moved together. Would take more time and images which I
will do when the weather permits. I had a terrible time figuring
out the stars. Guide8 stopped working and I didn't trust the
positions I imaged. I made one giff animation with two 6 minute
frames from a 1.5 hour period which I hope to post.(1.4mb)
Mike H.

Date:  Fri, 28 Nov 2008 15:49:25 -0000
From:  Bernhard Häusler 
Subject:  Some different views of one series of images: C/2006 W3 (Christensen) of Nov.27
Hi all,

last night was one of the best of the year. I took four comets with my
CCD camera in 12 hours total. And some of you followed the live
internet stream on my Comet Base until comet Ory... - so I got less
time to sleep.

Here is the first result of the evening, C2006W3 in 150 minutes total
exposure time. The comet is still showing a faint tail:

http://www.amication.de/Bernhards_Comet_Project/c2006w3.htm

clear skies
Bernhard

Hello Bernhard ,

In my list of observadorescometas of yahoogroups.com the photometry ccd of comets adjust of aperture radius depends on the size of the coma of the comet , we have method named( SYPHORA , SYstem of PHOtometry Radius Aperture ), MAXIM DL is good software for this method and new version of astroart ( v 4.0 ) .

Date:  Sat, 20 Dec 2008 20:53:13 -0000
From:  Bernhard Häusler 
Subject:  Re: 144P 2008-12-17.8922
Hello Stéphane,

thanks a lot for the allowance to work with your image!

this is the result:

A combination of two different lenses. The original image is taken
with a Audine Kaf 3200 ME ccd camera, settled on a 300 mm tele lens at
2008-12-17.
The inlay image is taken with a ST10XME ccd camera and the same chip,
settled on a 12" SCT f-7 telescope at 2008-12-19.

http://www.amication.de/Bernhards_Comet_Project/144p_20081217_19.htm

The quality of the 300 mm tele lens in combination with the Kaf 3200
ME is remarkable. Both methods, lo and hi resolution images of comets
have their own advantages.

Clear skies

Bernhard

http://www.amication.de/Bernhards_Comet_Project

Date:  Sun, 21 Dec 2008 11:11:31 +0100
From:  Bernd Häusler 
Subject:  AW: [Comet-Images] Re: 144P 2008-12-17.8922
Hello Mr. Harry Mays,

thank you very much for the compliment.

Yes, my telescope is working properly since 16 years now. In 2004 it fell
from my balcony during a thunderstorm. After a complete loop and a flight of
three meters it landed on the grass with the tripod below. The tripod was
damaged, but the scope was unhurt.

In progress of time I visited many telescope meetings and the scope was
transported over 10000 miles.

No, the only thing I can criticize are the screws, because they are a
little bit rusty after 16 years and the electrical plugs. Europe made scopes
are provided with plugs you can still use in 1000 years J. No joke, Meade
was the first company which provided computer controlled scopes for the
amateur for a very good price. And this happened at a time, when most of the
European amateurs had no internet, no personal computers and more than ever
no computerized scopes.

But to point out my attitude: I communicate on eye level with everybody and
many equipments are good for observing and photographing comets. I am an
amateur, but I like to work together with all comet lovers of the world.

Clear Skies and continue your good job too!

Bernhard

http://www.amication.de/Bernhards_Comet_Project/equipment.htm

Mr. Hausler, I too use the same scope and have for about the same duration

opinion you get a lot of bang for the buck. No complaints here! Your work is
fabulous. I do not know if you are a professional astronomer but your
results equal and exceed many pros using millions of dollars of equipment.
Tax payer paid for of course. Keep up the good work. Harry Mays Albany,

have their own advantages.

Date:  Fri, 26 Dec 2008 10:43:49 +0100
From:  Jose Pablo Navarro Pina 
Subject:  speed expansion comma outburts 29P/SW-1
Hi all , i calculate the speed expansion fo comma for latest outburts of comet 29P/SW-1 , estimate one speed aproximate for v. ~ 500 kms/h for this outburts , this is hight valor speed expansion for this comet normally outburts .

Images and graphics here :

http://webs.ono.com/jpab

Regards , J.P.Navarro Pina .
MPC-J70

[Non-text portions of this message have been removed] 

Date:  Fri, 26 Dec 2008 10:56:56 +0100
From:  Jose Pablo Navarro Pina 
Subject:  Re: [Comet-Images] speed expansion comma outburts 29P/SW-1
The method for the photometry ccd i used SYPHORA , we use aperture radius day 21/12 A.R. = 3 pix. m1 ( R USNO B1 ) = 11.6 , the day 25/12 A.R.= 8 pixels for the adjust coma box m1 ( R USNO B1 ) = 12.6 , we use the formula :

m R ( 3pix- 8pix. ) = mR (3pix.) -2.5 log ( 10e(0.4-dm1)-1.0)

the normally expansion speed relation Delsemme V bb = 0.58 * R (-0.5) , for this expresion my results of this outburts V bb = 0.138 kms s-1 .

Regards , J.P.Navarro Pina .

Date:  Sat, 27 Dec 2008 11:08:57 +1300
From:  John Drummond 
Subject:  29P (Schwassmann-Wachmann) imaged last night
Hi all,

I imaged 29P (Schwassmann-Wachmann) last night (Friday 26.625 December 2008 UT). I used a 41cm (16") @ f5.2 Meade Starfinder Newtonian and SBIG STL11000M CCD. 2 minute sublights - 6 x Lum, 3 x RGB. The FOV is cropped and about 15' x 15'. The coma is about 50" in diameter (in this image). North is up, East is left.

The colour seems to be set right. The lack of a normal greenish coma and having a pale coma (and the ball shape) reminds me of Comet Holmes (17P) from late 2007. This is my opinion and shouldn't be taken as a scientific statement...

http://www.possumobservatory.co.nz/comet_Schwassmann-Wachmann-29P-41cm@f4,5-2min-6xlum_3xrgb-20c-081226-web2.jpg
or
http://tinyurl.com/8z3nvd

Cheers

John Drummond
Possum Observatory (IAU Code: E94)
Gisborne, New Zealand
E 177° 53', S 38° 38'
Email: john_drummond@xtra.co.nz
Website: http://www.possumobservatory.co.nz
Images: http://www.possumobservatory.co.nz/latest_images-all-continuing.htm
